auditLog = logging.DefaultLogger.WithField(logfields.LogSubsys, \"policy-audit\")\n\n// PolicyAuditLogger provides structured logging of policy evaluation decisions\n// for audit and debugging purposes.\ntype PolicyAuditLogger struct {\n\tlock.Mutex\n\tlogLevel logrus.Level\n\tlogger   *logrus.Entry\n}\n\n// NewPolicyAuditLogger creates a new PolicyAuditLogger with the specified log level.\n// The logger is integrated with Cilium's logging framework.\nfunc NewPolicyAuditLogger(level logrus.Level) *PolicyAuditLogger {\n\treturn &PolicyAuditLogger{\n\t\tlogLevel: level,\n\t\tlogger:   auditLog,\n\t}\n}\n\n// LogDecision logs a policy verdict decision for a given identity and policy.\n// This is used to audit allow/deny decisions during policy evaluation.\nfunc (pal *PolicyAuditLogger) LogDecision(identity identity.NumericIdentity, policy string, verdict api.Decision, reason string) {\n\tpal.Lock()\n\tdefer pal.Unlock()\n\n\tif pal.logLevel < logrus.InfoLevel {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tscopedLog := pal.logger.WithFields(logrus.Fields{\n\t\tlogfields.Identity: identity,\n\t\t\"policy\":           policy,\n\t\t\"verdict\":          verdict.String(),\n\t\t\"reason\":           reason,\n\t})\n\n\tscopedLog.Info(\"Policy decision logged\")\n}\n\n// LogEvaluation logs the result of policy evaluation for a given policy key,\n// including selector cache interaction information.\nfunc (pal *PolicyAuditLogger) LogEvaluation(ctx context.Context, policyKey string, selectorCache *SelectorCache, result api.Decision) {\n\tpal.Lock()\n\tdefer pal.Unlock()\n\n\tif pal.logLevel < logrus.DebugLevel {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tscopedLog := pal.logger.WithFields(logrus.Fields{\n\t\tlogfields.PolicyKey: policyKey,\n\t\t\"decision\":          result.String(),\n\t})\n\n\tif selectorCache != nil {\n\t\tscopedLog = scopedLog.WithField(\"selector_cache_available\", true)\n\t}\n\n\tscopedLog.Debug(\"Policy evaluation completed\")\n}\n\n// SetLogLevel updates the log level for the PolicyAuditLogger.\nfunc (pal *PolicyAuditLogger) SetLogLevel(level logrus.Level) {\n\tpal.Lock()\n\tdefer pal.Unlock()\n\n\tpal.logLevel = level\n}\n\n// GetLogLevel returns the current log level of the PolicyAuditLogger.\nfunc (pal *PolicyAuditLogger) GetLogLevel() logrus.Level {\n\tpal.Lock()\n\tdefer pal.Unlock()\n\n\treturn pal.logLevel\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":8,"cache_creation_input_tokens":152,"cache_read_input_tokens":40414,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":152},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"e2b2b7fc-639e-4ecc-bf58-117d6a0ed3db","uuid":"ea58c300-32df-4e22-9766-c50490799abe"}

Pass each agent the full diff so it has the complete context.\n\n### Agent 1: Code Reuse Review\n\nFor each change:\n\n1. **Search for existing utilities and helpers** that could replace newly written code. Use Grep to find similar patterns elsewhere in the codebase — common locations are utility directories, shared modules, and files adjacent to the changed ones.\n2. **Flag any new function that handling, custom environment checks, ad-hoc type guards, and similar patterns are common candidates.\n\n### Agent 2: Code Quality Review\n\nReview the same changes for hacky patterns:\n\n1. **Redundant state**: state that duplicates existing state, cached values that could be derived, observers/effects that could be direct calls\n2. **Parameter sprawl**: adding new parameters to a function instead of generalizing or restructuring existing ones\n3. **Copy-paste with slight variation**: near-duplicate code blocks that should be unified with a shared abstraction\n4. **Leaky abstractions**: exposing internal details that should be encapsulated, or breaking existing abstraction boundaries\n5. **Stringly-typed code**: using raw strings where constants, enums (string unions), or branded types already exist in the codebase\n\n### Agent 3: Efficiency Review\n\nReview the same changes for efficiency:\n\n1. **Unnecessary work**: redundant computations, repeated file reads, duplicate network/API calls, N+1 patterns\n2. **Missed concurrency**: independent operations run sequentially when they could run in parallel\n3. **Hot-path bloat**: new blocking work added to startup or per-request/per-render hot paths\n4. **Unnecessary existence checks**: pre-checking file/resource existence before operating (TOCTOU anti-pattern) — operate directly and handle the error\n5. **Memory**: unbounded data structures, missing cleanup, event listener leaks\n6. **Overly broad operations**: reading entire files when only a portion is needed, loading all items when filtering for one\n\n## Phase 3: Fix Issues\n\nWait for all three agents to complete. 234→\t\tctx.PolicyTrace(\"Found unsatisfied FromRequires constraint\\n\")\n   235→\t} else {\n   236→\t\tif state.matchedRules > 0 {\n   237→\t\t\tctx.PolicyTrace(\"Found allow rule\\n\")\n   238→\t\t} else {\n   239→\t\t\tctx.PolicyTrace(\"Found no allow rule\\n\")\n   240→\t\t}\n   241→\t\tif state.matchedDenyRules > 0 {\n   242→\t\t\tctx.PolicyTrace(\"Found deny rule\\n\")\n   243→\t\t} 251→// Must only be called if using [NewStoppedPolicyRepository]\n   252→func (p *Repository) Start() {\n   253→\tp.RepositoryChangeQueue = option.Config.PolicyQueueSize)\n   255→\tp.RepositoryChangeQueue.Run()\n   256→\tp.RuleReactionQueue.Run()\n   257→}\n   258→\n   259→// ResolveL4IngressPolicy resolves the L4 ingress policy for a set of endpoints\n   260→// by searching the policy repository for `PortRule` rules that are attached to\n   261→// a `Rule` where the EndpointSelector matches `ctx.To`. `ctx.From` takes no effect and\n   262→// is ignored in the search.  If multiple `PortRule` rules are found, all rules\n   263→// are merged together. If rules contains overlapping port definitions, the first\n   264→// rule found in the repository takes precedence.\n   265→//\n   266→// TODO: Coalesce l7 rules?\n   267→//\n   268→// Caller must release resources by calling Detach() on the returned map!\n   269→//\n   270→// NOTE: This is only called from unit tests, but from multiple packages.\n   271→func (p *Repository) ResolveL4IngressPolicy(ctx *SearchContext) (L4PolicyMap, error) {\n   272→\tpolicyCtx := policyContext{\n   273→\t\trepo: p,\n   274→\t\tns:   ctx.To.Get(labels.LabelSourceK8sKeyPrefix + k8sConst.PodNamespaceLabel),\n   275→\t}\n   276→\trules := make(ruleSlice, 0, len(p.rules))\n   277→\tfor _, rule := range p.rules {\n   278→\t\trules = append(rules, rule)\n   279→\t}\n   280→\t// Sort for unit tests\n   281→\tslices.SortFunc[ruleSlice](rules, func(a, b *rule) int {\n   282→\t\treturn cmp.Compare(a.key.idx, b.key.idx)\n   283→\t})\n   284→\tresult, err := rules.resolveL4IngressPolicy(&policyCtx, ctx)\n   285→\tif err != nil {\n   286→\t\treturn nil, err\n   287→\t}\n   288→\n   289→\treturn result, nil\n   290→}\n   291→\n   292→// ResolveL4EgressPolicy resolves the L4 egress policy for a set of endpoints\n   293→// by searching the policy repository for `PortRule` rules that are attached to\n   294→// a `Rule` where the EndpointSelector matches `ctx.From`. `ctx.To` takes no effect and\n   295→// is ignored in the search.  If multiple `PortRule` rules are found, all rules\n   296→// are merged together. If rules contains overlapping port definitions, the first\n   297→// rule found in the repository takes precedence.\n   298→//\n   299→// Caller must release resources by calling Detach() on the returned map!\n   300→//\n   301→// NOTE: This is only called from unit tests, but from multiple packages.\n   302→func (p *Repository) ResolveL4EgressPolicy(ctx *SearchContext) (L4PolicyMap, error) {\n   303→\tpolicyCtx := policyContext{\n   304→\t\trepo: p,\n   305→\t\tns:   ctx.From.Get(labels.LabelSourceK8sKeyPrefix + k8sConst.PodNamespaceLabel),\n   306→\t}\n   307→\trules := make(ruleSlice, 0, len(p.rules))\n   308→\tfor _, rule := range p.rules {\n   309→\t\trules = append(rules, rule)\n   310→\t}\n   311→\tslices.SortFunc[ruleSlice](rules, func(a, b *rule) int {\n   312→\t\treturn cmp.Compare(a.key.idx, b.key.idx)\n   313→\t})\n   314→\tresult, err := rules.resolveL4EgressPolicy(&policyCtx, ctx)\n   315→\n   316→\tif err != nil {\n   317→\t\treturn nil, err\n   318→\t}\n   319→\n   320→\treturn result, nil\n   321→}\n   322→\n   323→// AllowsIngressRLocked evaluates the policy repository for the provided search\n   324→// context and returns the verdict for ingress. If no matching policy allows for\n   325→// the  connection, the request will be denied. The policy repository mutex must\n   326→// be held.\n   327→//\n   328→// NOTE: This is only called from unit tests, but from multiple packages.\n   329→func (p *Repository) AllowsIngressRLocked(ctx *SearchContext) api.Decision {\n   330→\t// Lack of DPorts in the SearchContext means L3-only search\n   331→\tif len(ctx.DPorts) == 0 {\n   332→\t\tnewCtx := *ctx\n   333→\t\tnewCtx.DPorts = []*models.Port{{\n   334→\t\t\tPort:     0,\n   335→\t\t\tProtocol: models.PortProtocolANY,\n   336→\t\t}}\n   337→\t\tctx = &newCtx\n   338→\t}\n   339→\n   340→\tctx.PolicyTrace(\"Tracing %s\", ctx.String())\n   341→\tingressPolicy, err := p.ResolveL4IngressPolicy(ctx)\n   342→\tif err != nil {\n   343→\t\tlog.WithError(err).Warn(\"Evaluation error while resolving L4 ingress policy\")\n   344→\t}\n   345→\n   346→\tverdict := api.Denied\n   347→\tif err == nil && ingressPolicy.Len() > 0 {\n   348→\t\tverdict = ingressPolicy.IngressCoversContext(ctx)\n   349→\t}\n   350→\n   351→\tctx.PolicyTrace(\"Ingress verdict: %s\", verdict.String())\n   352→\tingressPolicy.Detach(p.GetSelectorCache())\n   353→\n   354→\treturn verdict\n   355→}\n   356→\n   357→// AllowsEgressRLocked evaluates the policy repository for the provided search\n   358→// context and returns the verdict. If no matching policy allows for the\n   359→// connection, the request will be denied. The policy repository mutex must be\n   360→// held.\n   361→//\n   362→// NOTE: This is only called from unit tests, but from multiple packages.\n   363→func (p *Repository) AllowsEgressRLocked(ctx *SearchContext) api.Decision {\n   364→\t// Lack of DPorts in the SearchContext means L3-only search\n   365→\tif len(ctx.DPorts) == 0 {\n   366→\t\tnewCtx := *ctx\n   367→\t\tnewCtx.DPorts = []*models.Port{{\n   368→\t\t\tPort:     0,\n   369→\t\t\tProtocol: models.PortProtocolANY,\n   370→\t\t}}\n   371→\t\tctx = &newCtx\n   372→\t}\n   373→\n   374→\tctx.PolicyTrace(\"Tracing %s\\n\", ctx.String())\n   375→\tegressPolicy, err := p.ResolveL4EgressPolicy(ctx)\n   376→\tif err != nil {\n   377→\t\tlog.WithError(err).Warn(\"Evaluation error while resolving L4 egress policy\")\n   378→\t}\n   379→\tverdict := api.Denied\n   380→\tif err == nil && egressPolicy.Len() > 0 {\n   381→\t\tverdict = egressPolicy.EgressCoversContext(ctx)\n   382→\t}\n   383→\n   384→\tctx.PolicyTrace(\"Egress verdict: %s\", verdict.String())\n   385→\tegressPolicy.Detach(p.GetSelectorCache())\n   386→\treturn verdict\n   387→}\n   388→\n   389→// SearchRLocked searches the policy repository for rules which match the\n   390→// specified labels and will return an array of all rules which matched.\n   391→func (p *Repository) SearchRLocked(lbls labels.LabelArray) api.Rules {\n   392→\tresult := api.Rules{}\n   393→\n   394→\tfor _, r := range p.rules {\n   395→\t\tif r.Labels.Contains(lbls) {\n   396→\t\t\tresult = append(result, &r.Rule)\n   397→\t\t}\n   398→\t}\n   399→\n   400→\treturn result\n   401→}\n   402→\n   403→// AddListLocked inserts a rule into the policy repository with the repository already locked\n   404→// Expects that the entire rule list has already been sanitized.\n   405→func (p *Repository) AddListLocked(rules api.Rules) (ruleSlice, uint64) {\n   406→\tnewRules := make(ruleSlice, 0, len(rules))\n   407→\tfor _, r := range rules {\n   408→\t\tnewRule := p.newRule(*r, ruleKey{idx: p.nextID})\n   409→\t\tnewRules = append(newRules, newRule)\n   410→\t\tp.insert(newRule)\n   411→\t\tp.nextID++\n   412→\t}\n   413→\n   414→\treturn newRules, p.BumpRevision()\n   415→}\n   416→\n   417→// ReplaceByResourceLocked replaces all rules that belong to a given resource with a\n   418→// new set. The set of rules added and removed is returned, along with the new revision number.\n   419→// Resource must not be empty\n   420→func (p *Repository) ReplaceByResourceLocked(rules api.Rules, resource ipcachetypes.ResourceID) (newRules ruleSlice, oldRules ruleSlice, revision uint64) {\n   421→\tif len(resource) == 0 {\n   422→\t\t// This should never ever be hit, as the caller should have already validated the resource.\n   423→\t\t// However, if it does happen, it means something very wrong has happened and we are at risk\n   424→\t\t// of removing all network policies. So, we must panic rather than risk disabling network security.\n   425→\t\tpanic(\"may not replace API rules with an empty resource\")\n   426→\t}\n   427→\n   428→\tif old, ok := p.rulesByResource[resource]; ok {\n   429→\t\toldRules = make(ruleSlice, 0, len(old))\n   430→\t\tfor key, oldRule := range old {\n   431→\t\t\toldRules = append(oldRules, oldRule)\n   432→\t\t\tp.del(key)\n   433→\t\t}\n   434→\t}\n   435→\n   436→\tnewRules = make(ruleSlice, 0, len(rules))\n   437→\tif len(rules) > 0 {\n   438→\t\tp.rulesByResource[resource] = make(map[ruleKey]*rule, len(rules))\n   439→\t\tfor i, r := range rules {\n   440→\t\t\tnewRule := p.newRule(*r, ruleKey{resource: resource, idx: uint(i)})\n   441→\t\t\tnewRules = append(newRules, newRule)\n   442→\t\t\tp.insert(newRule)\n   443→\t\t}\n   444→\t}\n   445→\n   446→\treturn newRules, oldRules, p.BumpRevision()\n   447→}\n   448→\n   449→func (p *Repository) insert(r *rule) {\n   450→\tp.rules[r.key] = r\n   451→\trid := r.key.resource\n   452→\tif len(rid) > 0 {\n   453→\t\tif p.rulesByResource[rid] == nil {\n   454→\t\t\tp.rulesByResource[rid] = map[ruleKey]*rule{}\n   455→\t\t}\n   456→\t\tp.rulesByResource[rid][r.key] = r\n   457→\t}\n   458→\n   459→\tmetrics.Policy.Inc()\n   460→}\n   461→\n   462→func (p *Repository) del(key ruleKey) {\n   463→\tif p.rules[key] == nil {\n   464→\t\treturn\n   465→\t}\n   466→\tdelete(p.rules, key)\n   467→\n   468→\trid := key.resource\n   469→\tif len(rid) > 0 && p.rulesByResource[rid] != nil {\n   470→\t\tdelete(p.rulesByResource[rid], key)\n   471→\t\tif len(p.rulesByResource[rid]) == 0 {\n   472→\t\t\tdelete(p.rulesByResource, rid)\n   473→\t\t}\n   474→\t}\n   475→\tmetrics.Policy.Dec()\n   476→}\n   477→\n   478→// newRule allocates a CachedSelector for a given rule.\n   479→func (p *Repository) newRule(apiRule api.Rule, key ruleKey) *rule {\n   480→\tr := &rule{\n   481→\t\tRule: apiRule,\n   482→\t\tkey:  key,\n   483→\t}\n   484→\tr.subjectSelector, _ = p.selectorCache.AddIdentitySelector(r, r.Labels, *r.getSelector())\n   485→\treturn r\n   486→}\n   487→\n   488→// Release releases resources owned by a given rule slice.\n   489→// This is needed because we need to evaluate deleted rules after they\n   490→// are removed from the repository, so we must allow for a specific lifecycle\n   491→func (p *Repository) Release(rs ruleSlice) {\n   492→\tfor _, r := range rs {\n   493→\t\tif r.subjectSelector != nil {\n   494→\t\t\tp.selectorCache.RemoveSelector(r.subjectSelector, r)\n   495→\t\t}\n   496→\t}\n   497→}\n   498→\n   499→// MustAddList inserts a rule into the policy repository. It is used for\n   500→// unit-testing purposes only. Panics if the rule is invalid\n   501→func (p *Repository) MustAddList(rules api.Rules) (ruleSlice, uint64) {\n   502→\tfor i := range rules {\n   503→\t\t// FIXME(GH-31162): Many unit tests provide invalid rules\n   504→\t\terr := rules[i].Sanitize()\n   505→\t\tif err != nil {\n   506→\t\t\tpanic(err)\n   507→\t\t}\n   508→\t}\n   509→\tp.Mutex.Lock()\n   510→\tdefer p.Mutex.Unlock()\n   511→\treturn p.AddListLocked(rules)\n   512→}\n   513→\n   514→// Iterate iterates the policy repository, calling f for each rule. It is safe\n   515→// to execute Iterate concurrently.\n   516→func (p *Repository) Iterate(f func(rule *api.Rule)) {\n   517→\tp.Mutex.RWMutex.Lock()\n   518→\tdefer p.Mutex.RWMutex.Unlock()\n   519→\tfor _, r := range p.rules {\n   520→\t\tf(&r.Rule)\n   521→\t}\n   522→}\n   523→\n   524→// FindSelectedEndpoints finds all endpoints selected by a given ruleSlice.\n   525→// All endpoints that are selected will be added to endpointsToRegenerate; all\n   526→// endpoints that are *not* selected (but still valid) remain in endpointsToBumpRevision.\n   527→// policySelectionWG is done when all endpoints have been considered.\n   528→func (r ruleSlice) FindSelectedEndpoints(endpointsToBumpRevision, endpointsToRegenerate *EndpointSet, policySelectionWG *sync.WaitGroup) {\n   529→\tendpointsToBumpRevision.ForEachGo(policySelectionWG, func(epp Endpoint) {\n   530→\t\tsecurityIdentity, err := epp.GetSecurityIdentity()\n   531→\t\tif err != nil || securityIdentity == nil {\n   532→\t\t\t// The endpoint is no longer alive, or it does not have a security identity.\n   533→\t\t\t// We should remove it from the set of endpoints that will be bumped\n   534→\t\t\tendpointsToBumpRevision.Delete(epp)\n   535→\t\t\treturn\n   536→\t\t}\n   537→\t\tif r.matchesSubject(securityIdentity) {\n   538→\t\t\tendpointsToRegenerate.Insert(epp)\n   539→\t\t\tendpointsToBumpRevision.Delete(epp)\n   540→\t\t}\n   541→\t})\n   542→}\n   543→\n   544→// DeleteByLabelsLocked deletes all rules in the policy repository which\n   545→// contain the specified labels. Returns the revision of the policy repository\n   546→// after deleting the rules, as well as now many rules were deleted.\n   547→func (p *Repository) DeleteByLabelsLocked(lbls labels.LabelArray) (ruleSlice, uint64, int) {\n   548→\tdeletedRules := ruleSlice{}\n   549→\n   550→\tfor key, r := range p.rules {\n   551→\t\tif r.Labels.Contains(lbls) {\n   552→\t\t\tdeletedRules = append(deletedRules, r)\n   553→\t\t\tp.del(key)\n   554→\t\t}\n   555→\t}\n   556→\tl := len(deletedRules)\n   557→\n   558→\tif l > 0 {\n   559→\t\tp.BumpRevision()\n   560→\t}\n   561→\n   562→\treturn deletedRules, p.GetRevision(), l\n   563→}\n   564→\n   565→func (p *Repository) DeleteByResourceLocked(rid ipcachetypes.ResourceID) (ruleSlice, uint64) {\n   566→\trules := p.rulesByResource[rid]\n   567→\tif len(rules) == 0 {\n   568→\t\tdelete(p.rulesByResource, rid)\n   569→\t\treturn nil, p.GetRevision()\n   570→\t}\n   571→\n   572→\tdeletedRules := make(ruleSlice, 0, len(rules))\n   573→\tfor key, rule := range rules {\n   574→\t\tp.del(key)\n   575→\t\tdeletedRules = append(deletedRules, rule)\n   576→\t}\n   577→\n   578→\treturn deletedRules, p.BumpRevision()\n   579→}\n   580→\n   581→// DeleteByLabels deletes all rules in the policy repository which contain the\n   582→// specified labels\n   583→func (p *Repository) DeleteByLabels(lbls labels.LabelArray) (uint64, int) {\n   584→\tp.Mutex.Lock()\n   585→\tdefer p.Mutex.Unlock()\n   586→\t_, rev, numDeleted := p.DeleteByLabelsLocked(lbls)\n   587→\treturn rev, numDeleted\n   588→}\n   589→\n   590→// JSONMarshalRules returns a slice of policy rules as string in JSON\n   591→// representation\n   592→func JSONMarshalRules(rules api.Rules) string {\n   593→\tb, err := json.MarshalIndent(rules, \"\", \"  \")\n   594→\tif err != nil {\n   595→\t\treturn err.Error()\n   596→\t}\n   597→\treturn string(b)\n   598→}\n   599→\n   600→// GetJSON returns all rules of the policy repository as string in JSON\n   601→// representation\n   602→func (p *Repository) GetJSON() string {\n   603→\tp.Mutex.RLock()\n   604→\tdefer p.Mutex.RUnlock()\n   605→\n   606→\tresult := api.Rules{}\n   607→\tfor _, r := range p.rules {\n   608→\t\tresult = append(result, &r.Rule)\n   609→\t}\n   610→\n   611→\treturn JSONMarshalRules(result)\n   612→}\n   613→\n   614→// GetRulesMatching returns whether any of the rules in a repository contain a\n   615→// rule with labels matching the labels in the provided LabelArray.\n   616→//\n   617→// Must be called with p.Mutex held\n   618→func (p *Repository) GetRulesMatching(lbls labels.LabelArray) (ingressMatch bool, egressMatch bool) {\n   619→\tingressMatch = false\n   620→\tegressMatch = false\n   621→\tfor _, r := range p.rules {\n   622→\t\trulesMatch := r.getSelector().Matches(lbls)\n   623→\t\tif rulesMatch {\n   624→\t\t\tif len(r.Ingress) > 0 {\n   625→\t\t\t\tingressMatch = true\n   626→\t\t\t}\n   627→\t\t\tif len(r.IngressDeny) > 0 {\n   628→\t\t\t\tingressMatch = true\n   629→\t\t\t}\n   630→\t\t\tif len(r.Egress) > 0 {\n   631→\t\t\t\tegressMatch = true\n   632→\t\t\t}\n   633→\t\t\tif len(r.EgressDeny) > 0 {\n   634→\t\t\t\tegressMatch = true\n   635→\t\t\t}\n   636→\t\t}\n   637→\n   638→\t\tif ingressMatch && egressMatch {\n   639→\t\t\treturn\n   640→\t\t}\n   641→\t}\n   642→\treturn\n   643→}\n   644→\n   645→// NumRules returns the amount of rules in the policy repository.\n   646→//\n   647→// Must be called with p.Mutex held\n   648→func (p *Repository) NumRules() int {\n   649→\treturn len(p.rules)\n   650→}\n   651→\n   652→// GetRevision returns the revision of the policy repository\n   653→func (p *Repository) GetRevision() uint64 {\n   654→\treturn p.revision.Load()\n   655→}\n   656→\n   657→// Empty returns 'true' if repository has no rules, 'false' otherwise.\n   658→//\n   659→// Must be called without p.Mutex held\n   660→func (p *Repository) Empty() bool {\n   661→\tp.Mutex.Lock()\n   662→\tdefer p.Mutex.Unlock()\n   663→\treturn p.NumRules() == 0\n   664→}\n   665→\n   666→// BumpRevision allows forcing policy regeneration\n   667→func (p *Repository) BumpRevision() uint64 {\n   668→\tmetrics.PolicyRevision.Inc()\n   669→\treturn p.revision.Add(1)\n   670→}\n   671→\n   672→// GetRulesList returns the current policy\n   673→func (p *Repository) GetRulesList() *models.Policy {\n   674→\tp.Mutex.RLock()\n   675→\tdefer p.Mutex.RUnlock()\n   676→\n   677→\tlbls := labels.ParseSelectLabelArrayFromArray([]string{})\n   678→\truleList := p.SearchRLocked(lbls)\n   679→\n   680→\treturn &models.Policy{\n   681→\t\tRevision: int64(p.GetRevision()),\n   682→\t\tPolicy:   JSONMarshalRules(ruleList),\n   683→\t}\n   684→}\n   685→\n   686→// resolvePolicyLocked returns the selectorPolicy for the provided\n   687→// identity from the set of rules in the repository.  If the policy\n   688→// cannot be generated due to conflicts at L4 or L7, returns an error.\n   689→//\n   690→// Must be performed while holding the Repository lock.\n   691→func (p *Repository) resolvePolicyLocked(securityIdentity *identity.Identity) (*selectorPolicy, error) {\n   692→\t// First obtain whether policy applies in both traffic directions, as well\n   693→\t// as list of rules which actually select this endpoint. This allows us\n   694→\t// to not have to iterate through the entire rule list multiple times and\n   695→\t// perform the matching decision again when computing policy for each\n   696→\t// protocol layer, which is quite costly in terms of performance.\n   697→\tingressEnabled, egressEnabled,\n   698→\t\tmatchingRules :=\n   699→\t\tp.computePolicyEnforcementAndRules(securityIdentity)\n   700→\n   701→\tcalculatedPolicy := &selectorPolicy{\n   702→\t\tRevision:             p.GetRevision(),\n   703→\t\tSelectorCache:        p.GetSelectorCache(),\n   704→\t\tL4Policy:             NewL4Policy(p.GetRevision()),\n   705→\t\tIngressPolicyEnabled: ingressEnabled,\n   706→\t\tEgressPolicyEnabled:  egressEnabled,\n   707→\t}\n   708→\n   709→\tlbls := securityIdentity.LabelArray\n   710→\tingressCtx := SearchContext{\n   711→\t\tTo:          lbls,\n   712→\t\trulesSelect: true,\n   713→\t}\n   714→\n   715→\tegressCtx := SearchContext{\n   716→\t\tFrom:        lbls,\n   717→\t\trulesSelect: true,\n   718→\t}\n   719→\n   720→\tif option.Config.TracingEnabled() {\n   721→\t\tingressCtx.Trace = TRACE_ENABLED\n   722→\t\tegressCtx.Trace = TRACE_ENABLED\n   723→\t}\n   724→\n   725→\tpolicyCtx := policyContext{\n   726→\t\trepo: p,\n   727→\t\tns:   lbls.Get(labels.LabelSourceK8sKeyPrefix + k8sConst.PodNamespaceLabel),\n   728→\t}\n   729→\n   730→\tif ingressEnabled {\n   731→\t\tnewL4IngressPolicy, err := matchingRules.resolveL4IngressPolicy(&policyCtx, &ingressCtx)\n   732→\t\tif err != nil {\n   733→\t\t\treturn nil, err\n   734→\t\t}\n   735→\t\tcalculatedPolicy.L4Policy.Ingress.PortRules = newL4IngressPolicy\n   736→\t}\n   737→\n   738→\tif egressEnabled {\n   739→\t\tnewL4EgressPolicy, err := matchingRules.resolveL4EgressPolicy(&policyCtx, &egressCtx)\n   740→\t\tif err != nil {\n   741→\t\t\treturn nil, err\n   742→\t\t}\n   743→\t\tcalculatedPolicy.L4Policy.Egress.PortRules = newL4EgressPolicy\n   744→\t}\n   745→\n   746→\t// Make the calculated policy ready for incremental updates\n   747→\tcalculatedPolicy.Attach(&policyCtx)\n   748→\n   749→\treturn calculatedPolicy, nil\n   750→}\n   751→\n   752→// computePolicyEnforcementAndRules returns whether policy applies at ingress or ingress\n   753→// for the given security identity, as well as a list of any rules which select\n   754→// the set of labels of the given security identity.\n   755→//\n   756→// Must be called with repo mutex held for reading.\n   757→func (p *Repository) computePolicyEnforcementAndRules(securityIdentity *identity.Identity) (\n   758→\tingress, egress bool,\n   759→\tmatchingRules ruleSlice,\n   760→) {\n   761→\tlbls := securityIdentity.LabelArray\n   762→\n   763→\t// Check if policy enforcement should be enabled at the daemon level.\n   764→\tif lbls.Has(labels.IDNameHost) && !option.Config.EnableHostFirewall {\n   765→\t\treturn false, false, nil\n   766→\t}\n   767→\n   768→\tpolicyMode := GetPolicyEnabled()\n   769→\t// If policy enforcement isn't enabled, we do not enable policy\n   770→\t// enforcement for the endpoint. We don't care about returning any\n   771→\t// rules that match.\n   772→\tif policyMode == option.NeverEnforce {\n   773→\t\treturn false, false, nil\n   774→\t}\n   775→\n   776→\tmatchingRules = []*rule{}\n   777→\tfor _, r := range p.rules {\n   778→\t\tif r.matchesSubject(securityIdentity) {\n   779→\t\t\tmatchingRules = append(matchingRules, r)\n   780→\t\t}\n   781→\t}\n   782→\n   783→\t// If policy enforcement is enabled for the daemon, then it has to be\n   784→\t// enabled for the endpoint.\n   785→\t// If the endpoint has the reserved:init label, i.e. if it has not yet\n   786→\t// received any labels, always enforce policy (default deny).\n   787→\tif policyMode == option.AlwaysEnforce || lbls.Has(labels.IDNameInit) {\n   788→\t\treturn true, true, matchingRules\n   789→\t}\n   790→\n   791→\t// Determine the default policy for each direction.\n   792→\t//\n   793→\t// By default, endpoints have no policy and all traffic is allowed.\n   794→\t// If any rules select the endpoint, then the endpoint switches to a\n   795→\t// default-deny mode (same as traffic being enabled), per-direction.\n   796→\t//\n   797→\t// Rules, however, can optionally be configure to not enable default deny mode.\n   798→\t// If no rules enable default-deny, then all traffic is allowed except that explicitly\n   799→\t// denied by a Deny rule.\n   800→\t//\n   801→\t// There are three possible cases _per direction_:\n   802→\t// 1: No rules are present,\n   803→\t// 2: At least one default-deny rule is present. Then, policy is enabled\n   804→\t// 3: Only non-default-deny rules are present. Then, policy is enabled, but we must insert\n   805→\t//    an additional allow-all rule. We must do this, even if all traffic is allowed, because\n   806→\t//    rules may have additional effects such as enabling L7 proxy.\n   807→\thasIngressDefaultDeny := false\n   808→\thasEgressDefaultDeny := false\n   809→\tfor _, r := range matchingRules {\n   810→\t\tif !ingress || !hasIngressDefaultDeny { // short-circuit len()\n   811→\t\t\tif len(r.Ingress) > 0 || 52→\t\t\t\t// as ':' is not allowed within a k8s label, colons are represented\n    53→\t\t\t\t// with '-'.\n    54→\t\t\t\tcidr := strings.ReplaceAll(lbl.Key, \"-\", \":\")\n    55→\t\t\t\t_, netIP, 68→\treturn nil\n    69→}\n    70→\n    71→func getIdentityCache(ids identity.IdentityMap) scIdentityCache {\n    72→\tidCache := make(map[identity.NumericIdentity]scIdentity, len(ids))\n    73→\tfor nid, lbls := range ids {\n    74→\t\tidCache[nid] = newIdentity(nid, lbls)\n    75→\t}\n    76→\treturn idCache\n    77→}\n    78→\n    79→// userNotification stores the information needed to call\n    80→// IdentitySelectionUpdated callbacks to notify users of selector's\n    81→// identity changes. GetModel() models.SelectorCache {\n   120→\tsc.mutex.RLock()\n   121→\tdefer sc.mutex.RUnlock()\n   122→\n   123→\tselCacheMdl := make(models.SelectorCache, 0, len(sc.selectors))\n   124→\n   125→\tfor selector, idSel := range sc.selectors {\n   126→\t\tselections := idSel.GetSelections()\n   127→\t\tids := make([]int64, 0, len(selections))\n   128→\t\tfor i := range selections {\n   129→\t\t\tids = append(ids, int64(selections[i]))\n   130→\t\t}\n   131→\t\tselMdl := &models.SelectorIdentityMapping{\n   132→\t\t\tSelector:   selector,\n   133→\t\t\tIdentities: ids,\n   134→\t\t\tUsers:      int64(idSel.numUsers()),\n   135→\t\t\tLabels:     labelArrayToModel(idSel.GetMetadataLabels()),\n   136→\t\t}\n   137→\t\tselCacheMdl = append(selCacheMdl, selMdl)\n   138→\t}\n   139→\n   140→\treturn selCacheMdl\n   141→}\n   142→\n   143→func labelArrayToModel(arr labels.LabelArray) models.LabelArray {\n   144→\tlbls := make(models.LabelArray, 0, len(arr))\n   145→\tfor _, l := range arr {\n   146→\t\tlbls = append(lbls, &models.Label{\n   147→\t\t\tKey:    l.Key,\n   148→\t\t\tValue:  l.Value,\n   149→\t\t\tSource: l.Source,\n   150→\t\t})\n   151→\t}\n   152→\treturn 159→\t\t\tsc.userCond.Wait()\n   160→\t\t}\n   161→\t\t// get the current batch of notifications and release the lock so that SelectorCache\n   162→\t\t// can't block on userMutex while we call queueUserNotification(user CachedSelectionUser, selector CachedSelector, added, deleted []identity.NumericIdentity, wg *sync.WaitGroup) {\n   175→\tsc.startNotificationsHandlerOnce.Do(func() {\n   176→\t\tgo sc.handleUserNotifications()\n   177→\t})\n   178→\twg.Add(1)\n   179→\tsc.userMutex.Lock()\n   180→\tsc.userNotes = append(sc.userNotes, userNotification{\n   181→\t\tuser:     user,\n   182→\t\tselector: selector,\n   183→\t\tadded:    added,\n   184→\t\tdeleted:  deleted,\n   185→\t\twg:       wg,\n   186→\t})\n   187→\tsc.userMutex.Unlock()\n   188→\tsc.userCond.Signal()\n   189→}\n   190→\n   191→// NewSelectorCache creates a new SelectorCache with the given identities.\n   192→func NewSelectorCache(ids identity.IdentityMap) *SelectorCache {\n   193→\tsc := DESIGN ISSUE**\n\n**Locking strategy is over-protective and potentially problematic:**\n\n```go\ntype PolicyAuditLogger struct {\n    lock.Mutex\n    logLevel logrus.Level\n    logger   *logrus.Entry\n}\n\n// Every method locks\nfunc (pal *PolicyAuditLogger) LogDecision(...) {\n    pal.Lock()\n    defer pal.Unlock()\n    // ... actually uses logrus which is thread-safe\n}\n\nfunc (pal *PolicyAuditLogger) SetLogLevel(level logrus.Level) {\n    pal.Lock()\n    defer pal.Unlock()\n    pal.logLevel = level\n}\n\nfunc (pal *PolicyAuditLogger) GetLogLevel() logrus.Level {\n    pal.Lock()\n    defer pal.Unlock()\n    return pal.logLevel\n}\n```\n\n**Issues:**\n\na) **False sense of safety:** The lock protects reading `pal.logLevel`, but the comparison in line 43/63:\n```go\nif pal.logLevel < logrus.InfoLevel {  // Race condition possible\n    return\n}\nscopedLog := pal.logger.WithFields(...)  // logrus.Entry is thread-safe\n```\nis a classic TOCTOU (Time-Of-Check-Time-Of-Use) bug: You check logLevel while locked, but logLevel could change between the check and the log call.\n\nb) **Logrus is already thread-safe:** `logrus.Entry` methods are safe to call concurrently. The locks don't protect logrus operations.\n\nc) **Contention:** Every log call acquires the mutex, which creates a bottleneck.\n\nd) **Tests confirm the race:** The test at line 73-108 (`TestPolicyAuditLoggerThreadSafety`) runs 100 concurrent operations on each method, which would catch actual races. The test passes because `logrus` is thread-safe, not because the locking is necessary.\n\n**Pattern in similar code:**\n- `/workspace/pkg/policy/selectorcache.go` uses `lock.RWMutex` for complex shared data structures (line 94)\n- Simple logger state shouldn't use locks; let logrus handle concurrency\n\n**Recommendation:** Use `atomic.Value` or remove the mutex entirely. The log level check could use atomic operations.\n\n---\n\n### 7. **Logger Initialization - NAMING INCONSISTENCY**\n\n**Pattern inconsistency in Cilium:**\n\n```go\n// audit_logger.go (line 18) - uses \"auditLog\" (camelCase, specific)\nvar auditLog = logging.DefaultLogger.WithField(logfields.LogSubsys, \"policy-audit\")\n\n// api/selector.go (line 20) - uses \"log\" (simple)\nvar log = logging.DefaultLogger.WithField(logfields.LogSubsys, \"policy-api\")\n\n// groups/log.go (line 11-13) - uses \"log\" and stores subsystem separately\nvar (\n    subsystem = \"Groups\"\n    log       = logging.DefaultLogger.WithField(logfields.LogSubsys, subsystem)\n)\n```\n\n**Issues:**\n1. **Inconsistent naming:** `auditLog` vs `log` vs module-level pattern\n2. **Best practice in Cilium:** The standard pattern is `var log = logging.DefaultLogger.WithField(...)` (seen in selector.go, l4.go, config.go)\n3. **Using `auditLog`** stands out as non-standard and slightly verbose\n\n**Recommendation:** Rename to `var log` to match Cilium conventions. This is unnecessary because:\n- The global logger is immutable and doesn't change\n- Multiple instances all reference the same object\n- It creates a false sense that different loggers could have different targets\n- Adds indirection without benefit\n\n**Comparison:** Looking at `/workspace/pkg/policy/api/selector.go` (line 20), the pattern is to use a module-level logger (`var log = ...`) directly, which is simpler and clearer.\n\n---\n\n### 2. **Parameter Sprawl - MODERATE ISSUE**\n\n**Problem:** The `LogDecision` and `LogEvaluation` methods have scattered parameters that could be better structured:\n\n```go\n// Current - 4 separate parameters\nfunc (pal *PolicyAuditLogger) LogDecision(\n    identity identity.NumericIdentity,\n    policy string,\n    verdict api.Decision,\n    reason string)\n\n// Current - 4 separate parameters\nfunc (pal *PolicyAuditLogger) LogEvaluation(\n    ctx context.Context,\n    policyKey string,\n    selectorCache *SelectorCache,\n    result api.Decision)\n```\n\n**Issues:**\n- `LogDecision`: Mixing semantic types (NumericIdentity) with raw strings (\"policy\", \"reason\")\n- `LogEvaluation`: The `context` parameter is accepted but never used - suggests incomplete API design\n- No validation of string parameters (what's a valid policy name?)\n- Future extensions would add more parameters\n\n**Patterns in Cilium:**\n- Methods typically accept either a single context-like struct or well-typed parameters\n- The `SearchContext` in `/workspace/pkg/policy/policy.go` shows the pattern of bundling related parameters\n- Repository methods use focused parameter sets\n\n**Recommendation:** Consider creating small struct types:\n```go\ntype LogDecisionParams struct {\n    Identity identity.NumericIdentity\n    Policy   string\n    Verdict  api.Decision\n    Reason   string\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### 3. **Copy-Paste Code - ISSUE FOUND**\n\n**Pattern duplication in logging setup:**\n\n```go\n// LogDecision - lines 47-52\nscopedLog := pal.logger.WithFields(logrus.Fields{\n    logfields.Identity: identity,\n    \"policy\":           policy,\n    \"verdict\":          verdict.String(),\n    \"reason\":           reason,\n})\nscopedLog.Info(\"Policy decision logged\")\n\n// LogEvaluation - lines 67-76\nscopedLog := pal.logger.WithFields(logrus.Fields{\n    logfields.PolicyKey: policyKey,\n    \"decision\":          result.String(),\n})\nif selectorCache != nil {\n    scopedLog = scopedLog.WithField(\"selector_cache_available\", true)\n}\nscopedLog.Debug(\"Policy evaluation completed\")\n```\n\n**Issues:**\n- Both methods follow identical pattern: WithFields → conditional logic → log\n- The lock/unlock + level check pattern is duplicated in all 4 methods\n- Could be extracted to helper methods\n\n---\n\n### 4. **Leaky Abstractions - ISSUE FOUND**\n\n**Problems:**\n\na) **Exposing internal log level management:**\n```go\nfunc (pal *PolicyAuditLogger) SetLogLevel(level logrus.Level) { ... }\nfunc (pal *PolicyAuditLogger) GetLogLevel() logrus.Level { ... }\n```\n- Clients are forced to know about `logrus.Level` type\n- Forces runtime log level checking in methods (lines 43, 63)\n- Better pattern: Have logging happen unconditionally; let logging framework handle level filtering\n\nb) **Exposing SelectorCache parameter:**\n```go\nfunc (pal *PolicyAuditLogger) LogEvaluation(ctx context.Context, \n    policyKey string, \n    selectorCache *SelectorCache,  // <-- leaky\n    result api.Decision)\n```\n- Clients must pass the SelectorCache just to log a boolean flag\n- The logger only cares if it's nil or not\n- Tightly couples the logger to the SelectorCache type\n\nc) **Context parameter accepted but unused:**\n```go\nfunc (pal *PolicyAuditLogger) LogEvaluation(ctx context.Context, ...)\n    // ctx is never used in the function body\n```\n\n---\n\n### 5. **Stringly-Typed Code - ISSUE FOUND**\n\n**Raw string fields instead of constants/types:**\n\n```go\n// Line 49-51: Raw strings used as field names\n\"policy\":           policy,\n\"verdict\":          verdict.String(),\n\"reason\":           reason,\n\n// Line 69: Raw string field name\n\"decision\":          result.String(),\n\n// Line 73: Raw string field name\n\"selector_cache_available\", true\n```\n\n**Comparison to standards:**\n- `/workspace/pkg/policy/api/selector.go` uses `logfields.Identity`, `logfields.EndpointLabelSelector`\n- `/workspace/pkg/policy/audit_logger.go` properly uses `logfields.Identity` and `logfields.PolicyKey` in the logging calls\n- But other fields (\"policy\", \"reason\", \"verdict\", \"decision\", \"selector_cache_available\") are raw strings\n\n**Impact:**\n- Field names can diverge across the codebase inconsistently\n- Harder to search for logging of specific fields\n- No type safety or IDE autocomplete\n\n**Missing constants in logfields package:** The fields \"policy\", \"verdict\", \"reason\", \"decision\" should be defined in `/workspace/pkg/logging/logfields/logfields.go`.\n\n---\n\n### 6. **Thread Safety - DESIGN ISSUE**\n\n**Locking strategy is over-protective and potentially problematic:**\n\n```go\ntype PolicyAuditLogger struct {\n    lock.Mutex\n    logLevel logrus.Level\n    logger   *logrus.Entry\n}\n\n// Every method locks\nfunc (pal *PolicyAuditLogger) LogDecision(...) {\n    pal.Lock()\n    defer pal.Unlock()\n    // ... actually uses logrus which is thread-safe\n}\n\nfunc (pal *PolicyAuditLogger) SetLogLevel(level logrus.Level) {\n    pal.Lock()\n    defer pal.Unlock()\n    pal.logLevel = level\n}\n\nfunc (pal *PolicyAuditLogger) GetLogLevel() logrus.Level {\n    pal.Lock()\n    defer pal.Unlock()\n    return pal.logLevel\n}\n```\n\n**Issues:**\n\na) **False sense of safety:** The lock protects reading `pal.logLevel`, but the comparison in line 43/63:\n```go\nif pal.logLevel < logrus.InfoLevel {  // Race condition possible\n    return\n}\nscopedLog := pal.logger.WithFields(...)  // logrus.Entry is thread-safe\n```\nis a classic TOCTOU (Time-Of-Check-Time-Of-Use) bug: You check logLevel while locked, but logLevel could change between the check and the log call.\n\nb) **Logrus is already thread-safe:** `logrus.Entry` methods are safe to call concurrently. The locks don't protect logrus operations.\n\nc) **Contention:** Every log call acquires the mutex, which creates a bottleneck.\n\nd) **Tests confirm the race:** The test at line 73-108 (`TestPolicyAuditLoggerThreadSafety`) runs 100 concurrent operations on each method, which would catch actual races. The test passes because `logrus` is thread-safe, not because the locking is necessary.\n\n**Pattern in similar code:**\n- `/workspace/pkg/policy/selectorcache.go` uses `lock.RWMutex` for complex shared data structures (line 94)\n- Simple logger state shouldn't use locks; let logrus handle concurrency\n\n**Recommendation:** Use `atomic.Value` or remove the mutex entirely. The log level check could use atomic operations.\n\n---\n\n### 7. **Logger Initialization - NAMING INCONSISTENCY**\n\n**Pattern inconsistency in Cilium:**\n\n```go\n// audit_logger.go (line 18) - uses \"auditLog\" (camelCase, specific)\nvar auditLog = logging.DefaultLogger.WithField(logfields.LogSubsys, \"policy-audit\")\n\n// api/selector.go (line 20) - uses \"log\" (simple)\nvar log = logging.DefaultLogger.WithField(logfields.LogSubsys, \"policy-api\")\n\n// groups/log.go (line 11-13) - uses \"log\" and stores subsystem separately\nvar (\n    subsystem = \"Groups\"\n    log       = logging.DefaultLogger.WithField(logfields.LogSubsys, subsystem)\n)\n```\n\n**Issues:**\n1. **Inconsistent naming:** `auditLog` vs `log` vs module-level pattern\n2. **Best practice in Cilium:** The standard pattern is `var log = logging.DefaultLogger.WithField(...)` (seen in selector.go, l4.go, config.go)\n3. **Using `auditLog`** stands out as non-standard and slightly verbose\n\n**Recommendation:** Rename to `var log` to match Cilium conventions. If disambiguation is needed, use package naming (`policy.log`).\n\n---\n\n### 8. **Test Quality Issues**\n\n**In `audit_logger_test.go`:**\n\na) **Tests are superficial - they only verify \"no panic\":**\n```go\n// Line 32 - doesn't verify anything was logged\nlogger.LogDecision(identity, policy, verdict, reason)\n// Line 44 - doesn't verify log output\nlogger.LogEvaluation(ctx, policyKey, nil, result)\n```\n\nb) **No log output verification:** Tests don't capture and verify actual log messages\n\nc) **Context parameter not validated:** `ctx` is passed but tests never verify it's used correctly (it isn't)\n\nd) **Setup inconsistencies:** \n```go\n// Line 36: LogEvaluation test uses DebugLevel\nlogger := NewPolicyAuditLogger(logrus.DebugLevel)\n// Line 44: But Info level log call would fail to appear\nlogger.LogDecision(identity, \"policy\", api.Allowed, \"reason\")\n```\n\n---\n\n## Summary of Findings\n\n| Category | Severity | Issue |\n|----------|----------|-------|\n| Redundant State | Medium | `logger` field duplicates global `auditLog` |\n| Parameter Sprawl | Medium | Raw strings mixed with typed parameters; TOCTOU race condition in level check |\n| Logger Initialization | Low | Non-standard `auditLog` name vs Cilium's `log` convention |\n| Test Quality | Medium | Tests only verify no-panic; don't validate output |\n\n**Critical issues to address:**\n1. **Thread safety race condition** (level check + log is not atomic)\n2. **Leaky abstractions** (logrus.Level exposure, SelectorCache coupling)\n3. **Redundant logger field** (simplifies to using module-level `log`)"}],"totalDurationMs":44985,"totalTokens":37210,"totalToolUseCount":28,"usage":{"input_tokens":50,"cache_creation_input_tokens":337,"cache_read_input_tokens":33839,"output_tokens":2984,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":337,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}}}

In `selectorcache.go` (lines 397-399, 403-405), the `.WithFields()` calls are made directly on the log statement without intermediate variables, but the same inefficiency persists.\n\n**Impact:** Medium - If audit logging is enabled and called frequently, this creates unnecessary allocations and string conversions.\n\n---\n\n### 4.
